## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration in chemical reaction kinetics. The relationship typically follows rate laws where dA/dt depends on powers of concentration A, possibly with time-dependent terms for complex or photochemical reactions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Constant rate of consumption/production independent of concentration'}
- {'name': 'First-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)'}
- {'name': 'Second-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to square of concentration (bimolecular same-species reaction)'}
- {'name': 'nth-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'General power-law rate dependence on concentration'}
- {'name': 'Mixed-order / parallel reactions', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Simultaneous first and second order pathways'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'First-order forward and zero-order reverse (or approach to equilibrium)'}
- {'name': 'Reversible reaction with equilibrium', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * (A - c1)', 'scenario': 'First-order approach to equilibrium concentration c1'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Product-catalyzed reaction where product concentration is (c1 - A)'}
- {'name': 'Substrate inhibition kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2)', 'scenario': 'Enzyme kinetics with substrate inhibition at high concentrations'}
- {'name': 'Competitive product inhibition', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A * (1 + c2 * (c3 - A)))', 'scenario': 'Michaelis-Menten with product inhibition where product ~ c3 - A'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent decay rate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Reaction with time-varying rate constant (e.g., catalyst deactivation)'}
- {'name': 'Consecutive reaction intermediate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t)', 'scenario': 'Rate of intermediate species in consecutive A→B→C reactions'}
- {'name': 'Half-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5', 'scenario': 'Surface-mediated or diffusion-limited reactions'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Power-law concentration dependence → dA/dt = c * A^n indicates reaction order n, fundamental to rate law determination
- Linear dependence on A with nonzero intercept → suggests reversible reaction approaching equilibrium
- Quadratic in A with sign change → A*(c-A) form indicates autocatalytic or logistic-type kinetics
- Rational function of A → enzyme or surface-catalyzed mechanism with saturation
- Sum of exponentials in time → multiple parallel or consecutive reaction pathways
- Product of A and (constant - A) → conservation constraint where total concentration is fixed (closed system stoichiometry)
- Rate that changes sign at specific A value → equilibrium point; system approaches steady state from both directions
- Fractional power of A (e.g., A^0.5) → diffusion-limited or surface-reaction mechanism

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.16497856808125827*A**2 - 0.16497856808125827*A*exp(-0.012758725293544376*t) + 0.6208078669591699*sin(log(A + 1))`

The GT has three terms:
1. A quadratic term in A: `-0.165*A²`
2. An exponential decay term: `-0.165*A*exp(-0.01276*t)`
3. A sinusoidal term: `0.621*sin(log(A+1))`

Key basis functions: `A²`, `A*exp(αt)`, and `sin(log(A+1))`.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of these three basis functions.

**Critical observations:**
- The GT depends on both A and t
- It contains `sin(log(A+1))` - a very specific nonlinear function of A
- It contains `A*exp(ct)` - coupling A with exponential in t
- Most candidates won't have `sin(log(A+1))`

Let me quickly scan for candidates that have `sin(log(...))` with A inside:

Looking through all candidates... None of the candidates contain `sin(log(A + ...))`. Let me verify:

- Candidates with `sin(log(...))`: 17, 18, 40, 46, 58, 102 - but these have `log(c*t+1)` inside sin, not `log(A+1)`
- Candidates with `log(A*c + 1)`: 109, 112, 117, 124, 136 - but these aren't inside sin

The GT requires `sin(log(A+1))` which is a specific nonlinear function of A. No polynomial, exponential, or simple trigonometric function of A can reproduce this. By the principle of linear independence of basis functions, `sin(log(A+1))` cannot be expressed as any combination of `A^n`, `exp(A)`, `log(A+1)`, `A^0.5`, `sin(A)`, etc.

Let me double-check candidates that might have enough flexibility:

- **Candidate 79**: Has `sin(A*c5 + c6)` - this is `sin(linear in A)`, not `sin(log(A+1))`. NO MATCH.
- **Candidate 65, 66, 85, 88, 118**: Have `sin(A*c + c)` - same issue. NO MATCH.
- **Candidate 117**: Has `log(c4*exp(A*c5) + 1)` which is a softplus-like function of A, not sin(log(A+1)). NO MATCH.
- **Candidate 124**: Has `log(c5*exp(A*c6) + 1)` - same. NO MATCH.

None of the candidates contain the basis function `sin(log(A+c))` which is essential to match the GT. Since `sin(log(A+1))` is linearly independent from all other basis functions present in the candidates (polynomials in A, exponentials in A, sqrt(A), sin(A), log(A+1), etc.), no candidate can match.
